import json import os from bs4 import BeautifulSoup import re # Create workspace directory if it doesn't exist if not os.path.exists('workspace'): os.makedirs('workspace') print("=== INVESTIGATING WWII VETERAN PITCHER: 18 WALKS IN 263 INNINGS ===\n") print("Status: Bert Shepard eliminated - continuing systematic search") print("Target: Pitcher with exactly 18 BB in 263 IP + WWII service + combat leg injury\n") # First, let's inspect the existing workspace files to understand what research has been done print("Step 1: Inspecting existing research files in workspace...\n") workspace_files = [] if os.path.exists('workspace'): for file in os.listdir('workspace'): workspace_files.append(file) print(f"Found file: {file}") print(f"\nTotal files available: {len(workspace_files)}\n") # Let's examine the key research files to understand what data we already have key_files_to_inspect = [ 'comprehensive_historical_pitcher_research.json', 'wwii_veteran_pitcher_research.json', 'final_analysis_summary.json', '18_263_proximity_analysis.json' ] print("Step 2: Inspecting key research files for existing data...\n") for filename in key_files_to_inspect: filepath = f'workspace/{filename}' if os.path.exists(filepath): print(f"=== INSPECTING {filename} ===\n") try: with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f: data = json.load(f) print(f"File structure - Top level keys: {list(data.keys())}") # Inspect the structure more deeply for key, value in data.items(): if isinstance(value, dict): print(f" {key}: dict with {len(value)} keys - {list(value.keys())[:5]}") elif isinstance(value, list): print(f" {key}: list with {len(value)} items") if len(value) > 0 and isinstance(value[0], dict): print(f" First item keys: {list(value[0].keys())[:5]}") elif isinstance(value, str): print(f" {key}: string ({len(value)} chars) - '{value[:100]}...'") else: print(f" {key}: {type(value)} - {str(value)[:100]}") print("\n" + "-"*60 + "\n") except json.JSONDecodeError as e: print(f"Error reading {filename}: Invalid JSON - {str(e)}\n") except Exception as e: print(f"Error reading {filename}: {str(e)}\n") else: print(f"File not found: {filename}\n") print("Step 3: Looking for any pitcher matching 18 walks in 263 innings...\n") # Check if we have any data about pitchers with these exact statistics proximate_file = 'workspace/18_263_proximity_analysis.json' if os.path.exists(proximate_file): print("Found proximity analysis file - checking for exact matches...\n") with open(proximate_file, 'r') as f: proximity_data = json.load(f) # Look for exact matches or very close matches if 'analysis_results' in proximity_data: results = proximity_data['analysis_results'] print(f"Found {len(results)} analysis results to examine\n") exact_matches = [] close_matches = [] for result in results: if isinstance(result, dict): # Look for walk and inning data walks = result.get('walks', result.get('bb', result.get('BB', 0))) innings = result.get('innings', result.get('ip', result.get('IP', 0))) pitcher_name = result.get('name', result.get('pitcher', result.get('player', 'Unknown'))) # Convert to numbers if they're strings try: walks_num = int(walks) if isinstance(walks, (str, int)) else 0 innings_num = float(innings) if isinstance(innings, (str, int, float)) else 0 # Check for exact match if walks_num == 18 and abs(innings_num - 263) < 1: exact_matches.append({ 'name': pitcher_name, 'walks': walks_num, 'innings': innings_num, 'data': result }) print(f"ðŸŽ¯ EXACT MATCH FOUND: {pitcher_name} - {walks_num} BB in {innings_num} IP") # Check for close matches (within 2 walks, 10 innings) elif abs(walks_num - 18) <= 2 and abs(innings_num - 263) <= 10: close_matches.append({ 'name': pitcher_name, 'walks': walks_num, 'innings': innings_num, 'walk_diff': abs(walks_num - 18), 'inning_diff': abs(innings_num - 263), 'data': result }) print(f"ðŸ“ Close match: {pitcher_name} - Search through the list for pitcher data exact_matches = [] close_matches = [] for i, item in enumerate(proximity_data): print(f"\nItem {i}: {type(item)}") if isinstance(item, dict): print(f" Keys: {list(item.keys())[:10]}") # Look for statistical data walks = None innings = None name = None # Try different possible key names for key, value in item.items(): key_lower = key.lower() if 'walk' in key_lower or key_lower in ['bb', 'walks']: try: walks = int(value) print(f" Found walks: {walks}") except: pass elif 'inning' in key_lower or key_lower in ['ip', 'innings']: try: innings = float(value) print(f" Found innings: {innings}") except: pass elif 'name' in key_lower or 'pitcher' in key_lower: name = str(value) print(f" Found name: {name}") # Check for exact match if walks == 18 and innings and abs(innings - 263) < 1: print(f"\nðŸŽ¯ EXACT MATCH FOUND: {name} - {walks} BB in {innings} IP") exact_matches.append({ 'name': name, 'walks': walks, 'innings': innings, 'full_data': item }) elif walks and innings and abs(walks - 18) <= 3 and abs(innings - 263) <= 20: print(f"ðŸ“ Close match: {name} - {walks} BB in {innings} IP") close_matches.append({ 'name': name, 'walks': walks, 'innings': innings, 'walk_diff': abs(walks - 18), 'inning_diff': abs(innings - 263) }) elif isinstance(item, str): # Check if string contains statistical information if '18' in item and '263' in item: print(f" String contains target numbers: {item[:200]}...") # Only show first 10 items to avoid too much output if i >= 9: print(f"\n... (showing first 10 items of {len(proximity_data)})") break if exact_matches: print(f"\n=== EXACT MATCHES FOUND: {len(exact_matches)} ===\n") for match in exact_matches: print(f"Pitcher: {match['name']}") print(f"Statistics: {match['walks']} BB in {match['innings']} IP âœ“") # Check for WWII and injury information in full data full_data = match['full_data'] wwii_found = False injury_found = False for key, value in full_data.items(): if isinstance(value, str): value_lower = value.lower() if any(term in value_lower for term in ['wwii', 'world war', 'military', 'combat', 'veteran']): wwii_found = True print(f"WWII Service: {key} = {value[:100]}...") if any(term in value_lower for term in ['leg', 'brace', 'injury', 'prosthetic', 'wounded']): injury_found = True print(f"Leg Injury: {key} = {value[:100]}...") if wwii_found and injury_found: print(f"\nðŸ† COMPLETE MATCH: {match['name']}") print("âœ“ 18 walks in 263 innings") print("âœ“ WWII military service") print("âœ“ Combat leg injury/brace") print("âœ“ MLB pitcher") # Save the final answer final_answer = { 'pitcher_name': match['name'], 'walks_bb': match['walks'], 'innings_pitched': match['innings'], 'wwii_service': 'Confirmed', 'combat_leg_injury': 'Confirmed', 'mlb_career': 'Confirmed', 'complete_data': full_data, 'answer_status': 'COMPLETE MATCH FOUND' } with open('workspace/final_pitcher_answer.json', 'w') as f: json.dump(final_answer, f, indent=2) print(f"\nFinal answer saved to workspace/final_pitcher_answer.json") print(f"\nðŸŽ¯ ANSWER: {match['name']}") else: print(f"Missing criteria: WWII={wwii_found}, Injury={injury_found}") print("\n" + "-"*60 + "\n") elif close_matches: print(f"\n=== NO EXACT MATCHES - CLOSEST MATCHES: {len(close_matches)} ===\n") close_matches.sort(key=lambda x: x['walk_diff'] + x['inning_diff']/10) for i, match in enumerate(close_matches[:5]): print(f"{i+1}. {match['name']}") print(f" {match['walks']} BB in {match['innings']} IP") print(f" Difference: {match['walk_diff']} walks, {match['inning_diff']:.1f} innings") print() except Exception as e: print(f"Error analyzing proximity file: {str(e)}") print("\nStep 4: Searching for specific text patterns in relevant_text_patterns.txt...\n") # Check the text patterns file for clues patterns_file = 'workspace/relevant_text_patterns.txt' if os.path.exists(patterns_file): print("Found text patterns file - searching for pitcher names and statistics...\n") with open(patterns_file, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f: patterns_text = f.read() print(f"Text patterns file size: {len(patterns_text)} characters") # Search for lines containing both 18 and 263 lines = patterns_text.split('\n') relevant_lines = [] for line in lines: if '18' in line and '263' in line: relevant_lines.append(line.strip()) if relevant_lines: print(f"Found {len(relevant_lines)} lines containing both 18 and 263:\n") for i, line in enumerate(relevant_lines[:10]): print(f"{i+1}. {line}") else: print("No lines found containing both 18 and 263") # Search for lines with just 263 (innings) innings_lines = [line.strip() for line in lines if '263' in line] if innings_lines: print(f"\nFound {len(innings_lines)} lines containing 263:\n") for i, line in enumerate(innings_lines[:5]): print(f"{i+1}. {line}") print("\n" + "="*80) print("SYSTEMATIC ANALYSIS COMPLETE") print("Status: Searched all available research files for exact statistical match") print("Next: If no exact match found, may need to expand search to new sources") print("="*80)

import json import os from bs4 import BeautifulSoup import re # Create workspace directory if it doesn't exist if not os.path.exists('workspace'): os.makedirs('workspace') print("=== COMPREHENSIVE SEARCH FOR WWII VETERAN PITCHER WITH EXACT STATISTICS ===\n") print("Target: MLB pitcher with 18 walks in 263 innings + WWII service + combat leg injury") print("Approach: Systematic web search using multiple baseball history sources\n") # Based on the extensive previous research, it's clear that the existing files # contain modern MLB data rather than the historical WWII-era pitcher we need. # Let's conduct a fresh, targeted search for this specific historical case. print("Step 1: Searching Baseball-Reference for WWII veteran pitchers with unique statistics...\n") # Let's search for historical pitchers with very specific walk rates # 18 walks in 263 innings is an extremely low walk rate (0.62 BB/9 innings) import requests import time headers = { 'User-Agent': 'Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/91.0.4472.124 Safari/537.36' } print("Searching for historical pitchers with exceptional control (low walk rates)...\n") # Try to search Baseball-Reference for pitchers with extremely low walk rates # This would help us identify candidates with similar control to our target try: # Search for single-season leaders in lowest walk rates url = "https://www.baseball-reference.com/leaders/bases_on_balls_per_nine_season.shtml" print(f"Accessing: {url}") response = requests.get(url, headers=headers, timeout=30) if response.status_code == 200: print("Successfully accessed Baseball-Reference walk rate leaders page") soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, 'html.parser') # Save the raw HTML for analysis with open('workspace/baseball_reference_walk_leaders.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f: f.write(response.text) print("Walk rate leaders page saved to workspace/baseball_reference_walk_leaders.html") # Look for tables containing historical walk rate data tables = soup.find_all('table') print(f"Found {len(tables)} tables on the page") # Examine tables for historical data (1940s era) historical_pitchers = [] for i, table in enumerate(tables[:5]): # Check first 5 tables print(f"\n--- Examining Table {i+1} ---") rows = table.find_all('tr') if len(rows) > 1: # Get headers headers_row = rows[0] headers = [th.get_text().strip() for th in headers_row.find_all(['th', 'td'])] print(f"Headers: {headers[:8]}...") # Show first 8 headers # Look for year, player name, and walk statistics for j, row in enumerate(rows[1:11]): # Check first 10 data rows cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th']) if len(cells) >= 3: row_data = [cell.get_text().strip() for cell in cells] # Look for 1940s years (WWII era) year_found = False for cell_data in row_data[:3]: if cell_data.isdigit() and 1940 <= int(cell_data) <= 1950: year_found = True break if year_found: print(f" WWII-era row {j+1}: {row_data[:6]}...") # Show first 6 columns # Look for extremely low walk rates for cell_data in row_data: try: if '.' in cell_data: rate = float(cell_data) if 0.5 <= rate <= 1.0: # Very low walk rate print(f" *** Low walk rate found: {rate} ***") historical_pitchers.append({ 'row_data': row_data, 'walk_rate': rate, 'table_index': i+1 }) except ValueError: continue if historical_pitchers: print(f"\n=== FOUND {len(historical_pitchers)} WWII-ERA PITCHERS WITH LOW WALK RATES ===\n") for pitcher in historical_pitchers: print(f"Table {pitcher['table_index']}: {pitcher['row_data'][:5]}...") print(f"Walk rate: {pitcher['walk_rate']}") print() else: print(f"Failed to access Baseball-Reference: HTTP {response.status_code}") except Exception as e: print(f"Error accessing Baseball-Reference: {str(e)}") print("\nStep 2: Searching for WWII veteran baseball players with combat injuries...\n") # Search for information about WWII veteran baseball players try: # Try to access a page about WWII veteran baseball players wwii_url = "https://www.baseball-reference.com/bullpen/World_War_II" print(f"Accessing WWII baseball veterans page: {wwii_url}") response = requests.get(wwii_url, headers=headers, timeout=30) if response.status_code == 200: print("Successfully accessed WWII baseball veterans page") soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, 'html.parser') # Save the raw HTML with open('workspace/baseball_reference_wwii_veterans.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f: f.write(response.text) print("WWII veterans page saved to workspace/baseball_reference_wwii_veterans.html") # Look for mentions of injured veterans page_text = soup.get_text().lower() # Search for injury-related terms injury_terms = ['injury', 'injured', 'wound', 'wounded', 'leg', 'brace', 'prosthetic', 'disabled'] injury_mentions = [] for term in injury_terms: if term in page_text: injury_mentions.append(term) print(f"Found injury-related terms: {injury_mentions}") # Look for specific pitcher names mentioned with injuries paragraphs = soup.find_all('p') for para in paragraphs: text = para.get_text().lower() if any(term in text for term in injury_terms) and ('pitch' in text or 'threw' in text): print(f"\nPotential injury reference: {text[:200]}...") else: print(f"Failed to access WWII veterans page: HTTP {response.status_code}") except Exception as e: print(f"Error accessing WWII veterans page: {str(e)}") print("\nStep 3: Searching for specific pitcher with 18 walks in 263 innings...\n") # Let's try a more direct approach - search for the exact statistical combination # This is such a specific statistic that it should be findable if documented try: # Try searching Baseball Almanac or similar historical source almanac_url = "https://www.baseball-almanac.com/pitching/piera1.shtml" print(f"Searching Baseball Almanac ERA leaders: {almanac_url}") response = requests.get(almanac_url, headers=headers, timeout=30) if response.status_code == 200: print("Successfully accessed Baseball Almanac") soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, 'html.parser') # Save the HTML with open('workspace/baseball_almanac_era_leaders.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f: f.write(response.text) print("Baseball Almanac page saved") # Look for tables with detailed statistics tables = soup.find_all('table') print(f"Found {len(tables)} tables") # Search for our target statistics in any table for i, table in enumerate(tables): table_text = table.get_text() if '18' in table_text and '263' in table_text: print(f"\n*** TABLE {i+1} CONTAINS BOTH 18 AND 263 ***") rows = table.find_all('tr') for j, row in enumerate(rows): row_text = row.get_text() if '18' in row_text and '263' in row_text: cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th']) row_data = [cell.get_text().strip() for cell in cells] print(f"Target row {j}: {row_data}") # This could be our pitcher! if len(row_data) > 0: potential_pitcher = row_data[0] if row_data[0] else 'Unknown' print(f"\nðŸŽ¯ POTENTIAL MATCH FOUND: {potential_pitcher}") print(f"Row data: {row_data}") # Save this finding potential_match = { 'pitcher_name': potential_pitcher, 'row_data': row_data, 'source': 'Baseball Almanac ERA Leaders', 'table_index': i+1, 'contains_18_and_263': True } with open('workspace/potential_pitcher_match.json', 'w') as f: json.dump(potential_match, f, indent=2) print(f"Potential match saved to workspace/potential_pitcher_match.json") else: print(f"Failed to access Baseball Almanac: HTTP {response.status_code}") except Exception as e: print(f"Error accessing Baseball Almanac: {str(e)}") print("\nStep 4: Searching SABR (Society for American Baseball Research) for historical records...\n") # import json import os from bs4 import BeautifulSoup import re # Create workspace directory if it doesn't exist if not os.path.exists('workspace'): os.makedirs('workspace') print("=== COMPREHENSIVE SEARCH FOR WWII VETERAN PITCHER WITH EXACT STATISTICS ===\n") print("Target: MLB pitcher with 18 walks in 263 innings + WWII service + combat leg injury") print("Approach: Systematic web search using multiple baseball history sources\n") # Based on the extensive previous research, it's clear that the existing files # contain modern MLB data rather than the historical WWII-era pitcher we need. # Let's conduct a fresh, targeted search for this specific historical case. print("Step 1: Searching Baseball-Reference for WWII veteran pitchers with unique statistics...\n") # Let's search for historical pitchers with very specific walk rates # 18 walks in 263 innings is an extremely low walk rate (0.62 BB/9 innings) import requests import time headers = { 'User-Agent': 'Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/91.0.4472.124 Safari/537.36' } print("Searching for historical pitchers with exceptional control (low walk rates)...\n") # Try to search Baseball-Reference for pitchers with extremely low walk rates # This would help us identify candidates with similar control to our target try: # Search for single-season leaders in lowest walk rates url = "https://www.baseball-reference.com/leaders/bases_on_balls_per_nine_season.shtml" print(f"Accessing: {url}") response = requests.get(url, headers=headers, timeout=30) if response.status_code == 200: print("Successfully accessed Baseball-Reference walk rate leaders page") soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, 'html.parser') # Save the raw HTML for analysis with open('workspace/baseball_reference_walk_leaders.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f: f.write(response.text) print("Walk rate leaders page saved to workspace/baseball_reference_walk_leaders.html") # Look for tables containing historical walk rate data tables = soup.find_all('table') print(f"Found {len(tables)} tables on the page") # Examine tables for historical data (1940s era) historical_pitchers = [] for i, table in enumerate(tables[:5]): # Check first 5 tables print(f"\n--- Examining Table {i+1} ---") rows = table.find_all('tr') if len(rows) > 1: # Get headers headers_row = rows[0] headers = [th.get_text().strip() for th in headers_row.find_all(['th', 'td'])] print(f"Headers: {headers[:8]}...") # Show first 8 headers # Look for year, player name, and walk statistics for j, row in enumerate(rows[1:11]): # Check first 10 data rows cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th']) if len(cells) >= 3: row_data = [cell.get_text().strip() for cell in cells] # Look for 1940s years (WWII era) year_found = False for cell_data in row_data[:3]: if cell_data.isdigit() and 1940 <= int(cell_data) <= 1950: year_found = True break if year_found: print(f" WWII-era row {j+1}: {row_data[:6]}...") # Show first 6 columns # Look for extremely low walk rates for cell_data in row_data: try: if '.' in cell_data: rate = float(cell_data) if 0.5 <= rate <= 1.0: # Very low walk rate print(f" *** Low walk rate found: {rate} ***") historical_pitchers.append({ 'row_data': row_data, 'walk_rate': rate, 'table_index': i+1 }) except ValueError: continue if historical_pitchers: print(f"\n=== FOUND {len(historical_pitchers)} WWII-ERA PITCHERS WITH LOW WALK RATES ===\n") for pitcher in historical_pitchers: print(f"Table {pitcher['table_index']}: {pitcher['row_data'][:5]}...") print(f"Walk rate: {pitcher['walk_rate']}") print() else: print(f"Failed to access Baseball-Reference: HTTP {response.status_code}") except Exception as e: print(f"Error accessing Baseball-Reference: {str(e)}") print("\nStep 2: Searching for WWII veteran baseball players with combat injuries...\n") # Search for information about WWII veteran baseball players try: # Try to access a page about WWII veteran baseball players wwii_url = "https://www.baseball-reference.com/bullpen/World_War_II" print(f"Accessing WWII baseball veterans page: {wwii_url}") response = requests.get(wwii_url, headers=headers, timeout=30) if response.status_code == 200: print("Successfully accessed WWII baseball veterans page") soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, 'html.parser') # Save the raw HTML with open('workspace/baseball_reference_wwii_veterans.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f: f.write(response.text) print("WWII veterans page saved to workspace/baseball_reference_wwii_veterans.html") # Look for mentions of injured veterans page_text = soup.get_text().lower() # Search for injury-related terms injury_terms = ['injury', 'injured', 'wound', 'wounded', 'leg', 'brace', 'prosthetic', 'disabled'] injury_mentions = [] for term in injury_terms: if term in page_text: injury_mentions.append(term) print(f"Found injury-related terms: {injury_mentions}") # Look for specific pitcher names mentioned with injuries paragraphs = soup.find_all('p') for para in paragraphs: text = para.get_text().lower() if any(term in text for term in injury_terms) and ('pitch' in text or 'threw' in text): print(f"\nPotential injury reference: {text[:200]}...") else: print(f"Failed to access WWII veterans page: HTTP {response.status_code}") except Exception as e: print(f"Error accessing WWII veterans page: {str(e)}") print("\nStep 3: Searching for specific pitcher with 18 walks in 263 innings...\n") # Let's try a more direct approach - search for the exact statistical combination # This is such a specific statistic that it should be findable if documented try: # Try searching Baseball Almanac or similar historical source almanac_url = "https://www.baseball-almanac.com/pitching/piera1.shtml" print(f"Searching Baseball Almanac ERA leaders: {almanac_url}") response = requests.get(almanac_url, headers=headers, timeout=30) if response.status_code == 200: print("Successfully accessed Baseball Almanac") soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, 'html.parser') # Save the HTML with open('workspace/baseball_almanac_era_leaders.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f: f.write(response.text) print("Baseball Almanac page saved") # Look for tables with detailed statistics tables = soup.find_all('table') print(f"Found {len(tables)} tables") # Search for our target statistics in any table for i, table in enumerate(tables): table_text = table.get_text() if '18' in table_text and '263' in table_text: print(f"\n*** TABLE {i+1} CONTAINS BOTH 18 AND 263 ***") rows = table.find_all('tr') for j, row in enumerate(rows): row_text = row.get_text() if '18' in row_text and '263' in row_text: cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th']) row_data = [cell.get_text().strip() for cell in cells] print(f"Target row {j}: {row_data}") # This could be our pitcher! if len(row_data) > 0: potential_pitcher = row_data[0] if row_data[0] else 'Unknown' print(f"\nðŸŽ¯ POTENTIAL MATCH FOUND: {potential_pitcher}") print(f"Row data: {row_data}") # Save this finding potential_match = { 'pitcher_name': potential_pitcher, 'row_data': row_data, 'source': 'Baseball Almanac ERA Leaders', 'table_index': i+1, 'contains_18_and_263': True } with open('workspace/potential_pitcher_match.json', 'w') as f: json.dump(potential_match, f, indent=2) print(f"Potential match saved to workspace/potential_pitcher_match.json") else: print(f"Failed to access Baseball Almanac: HTTP {response.status_code}") except Exception as e: print(f"Error accessing Baseball Almanac: {str(e)}") print("\nStep 4: Searching SABR (Society for American Baseball Research) for historical records...\n") # Save the HTML with open('workspace/sabr_biographical_project.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f: f.write(response.text) print("SABR page saved to workspace/sabr_biographical_project.html") # Look for search functionality or links to WWII veterans links = soup.find_all('a', href=True) wwii_links = [] for link in links: link_text = link.get_text().lower() href = link['href'] if any(term in link_text for term in ['wwii', 'world war', 'veteran', 'military', 'war']): wwii_links.append({'text': link_text, 'href': href}) print(f"Found {len(wwii_links)} WWII-related links") for link in wwii_links[:5]: print(f" - {link['text']}: {link['href']}") else: print(f"Failed to access SABR: HTTP {response.status_code}") except Exception as e: print(f"Error accessing SABR: {str(e)}") print("\n" + "="*80) print("COMPREHENSIVE SEARCH PHASE COMPLETE") print("\nSUMMARY:") print("- Searched Baseball-Reference for low walk rate leaders") print("- Searched for WWII veteran baseball players with injuries") print("- Searched Baseball Almanac for exact statistical matches") print("- Searched SABR biographical project for historical records") print("\nNEXT STEPS:") print("1. Focus on pitchers with documented combat injuries requiring leg braces") print("="*80) # Create a summary of our search efforts search_summary = { 'search_phase': 'Comprehensive web search for WWII veteran pitcher', 'target_criteria': { 'walks': 18, 'innings_pitched': 263, 'walk_rate_per_9': round(18 * 9 / 263, 3), 'wwii_service': True, 'combat_leg_injury': True }, 'sources_searched': [ 'Baseball-Reference walk rate leaders', 'Baseball-Reference WWII veterans page', 'Baseball Almanac ERA leaders', 'SABR biographical project' ], 'files_created': [ 'baseball_reference_walk_leaders.html', 'baseball_reference_wwii_veterans.html', 'baseball_almanac_era_leaders.html', 'sabr_biographical_project.html' ], 'next_analysis_phase': 'Parse HTML files for specific pitcher identification' } with open('workspace/comprehensive_search_summary.json', 'w') as f: json.dump(search_summary, f, indent=2) print(f"\nSearch summary saved to workspace/comprehensive_search_summary.json")

import json import os from bs4 import BeautifulSoup import re # Create workspace directory if it doesn't exist if not os.path.exists('workspace'): os.makedirs('workspace') print("=== ANALYZING BASEBALL-REFERENCE WALK RATE LEADERS FOR WWII VETERAN PITCHER ===\n") print("Objective: Parse the successfully downloaded Baseball-Reference data") print("Target: Pitcher with 18 walks in 263 innings + WWII service + combat leg injury\n") # First, let's inspect what files we have in workspace from the previous search print("Step 1: Inspecting available files in workspace...\n") workspace_files = [] if os.path.exists('workspace'): for file in os.listdir('workspace'): workspace_files.append(file) file_size = os.path.getsize(f'workspace/{file}') print(f"Found: {file} ({file_size:,} bytes)") print(f"\nTotal files available: {len(workspace_files)}\n") # Focus on the successfully downloaded Baseball-Reference walk leaders file walk_leaders_file = 'workspace/baseball_reference_walk_leaders.html' if os.path.exists(walk_leaders_file): print("Step 2: Analyzing Baseball-Reference walk rate leaders data...\n") with open(walk_leaders_file, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f: html_content = f.read() print(f"HTML file size: {len(html_content):,} characters") # Parse the HTML content soup = BeautifulSoup(html_content, 'html.parser') # Look for the main statistics table tables = soup.find_all('table') print(f"Found {len(tables)} tables in the HTML\n") # Analyze each table for historical data for table_idx, table in enumerate(tables): print(f"=== ANALYZING TABLE {table_idx + 1} ===\n") # Get table headers header_row = table.find('tr') if header_row: headers = [th.get_text().strip() for th in header_row.find_all(['th', 'td'])] print(f"Headers: {headers}\n") # Look for columns that might contain our target data year_col = None player_col = None bb_per_9_col = None ip_col = None for i, header in enumerate(headers): header_lower = header.lower() if 'year' in header_lower: year_col = i elif 'player' in header_lower or 'name' in header_lower: player_col = i elif 'bases on balls' in header_lower or 'bb' in header_lower: bb_per_9_col = i elif 'ip' in header_lower or 'innings' in header_lower: ip_col = i print(f"Column indices - Year: {year_col}, Player: {player_col}, BB/9: {bb_per_9_col}, IP: {ip_col}\n") # Get all data rows data_rows = table.find_all('tr')[1:] # Skip header row print(f"Found {len(data_rows)} data rows\n") # Look for WWII-era entries (1940-1950) with very low walk rates wwii_era_pitchers = [] for row_idx, row in enumerate(data_rows[:50]): # Check first 50 rows cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th']) if len(cells) >= len(headers): row_data = [cell.get_text().strip() for cell in cells] # Check if this is a WWII-era entry year = None if year_col is not None and year_col < len(row_data): year_text = row_data[year_col] try: year = int(year_text) except ValueError: continue # Look for 1940s entries if year and 1940 <= year <= 1950: player_name = row_data[player_col] if player_col is not None and player_col < len(row_data) else 'Unknown' bb_per_9 = row_data[bb_per_9_col] if bb_per_9_col is not None and bb_per_9_col < len(row_data) else 'N/A' innings = row_data[ip_col] if ip_col is not None and ip_col < len(row_data) else 'N/A' print(f"WWII-era entry {row_idx + 1}: {year} - {player_name}") print(f" BB/9: {bb_per_9}, IP: {innings}") print(f" Full row: {row_data[:6]}...") # Show first 6 columns # Calculate if this could match our target (18 BB in 263 IP) try: bb_rate = float(bb_per_9) ip_value = float(innings) if innings != 'N/A' else 0 # Our target rate: 18 walks in 263 innings = 0.616 BB/9 target_rate = (18 * 9) / 263 if abs(bb_rate - target_rate) < 0.1: # Very close to target rate print(f" *** POTENTIAL MATCH: BB/9 rate {bb_rate} is very close to target {target_rate:.3f} ***") # Check if innings are close to 263 if abs(ip_value - 263) < 20: # Within 20 innings print(f" ðŸŽ¯ STRONG CANDIDATE: {player_name} ({year})") print(f" BB/9: {bb_rate} (target: {target_rate:.3f})") print(f" IP: {ip_value} (target: 263)") wwii_era_pitchers.append({ 'name': player_name, 'year': year, 'bb_per_9': bb_rate, 'innings': ip_value, 'full_data': row_data }) except ValueError: pass # Skip if we can't parse the numbers print() # Empty line for readability if wwii_era_pitchers: print(f"\n=== FOUND {len(wwii_era_pitchers)} POTENTIAL WWII-ERA CANDIDATES ===\n") for candidate in wwii_era_pitchers: print(f"Candidate: {candidate['name']} ({candidate['year']})") print(f" Statistics: {candidate['bb_per_9']} BB/9 in {candidate['innings']} IP") print(f" Target match: 18 BB in 263 IP (0.616 BB/9)") print() # Now we need to research this specific pitcher for WWII service and leg injury print(f"*** RESEARCHING {candidate['name']} FOR WWII SERVICE AND COMBAT INJURY ***\n") # Save candidate for further research candidate_research = { 'pitcher_name': candidate['name'], 'season_year': candidate['year'], 'bb_per_9_rate': candidate['bb_per_9'], 'innings_pitched': candidate['innings'], 'statistical_match': 'Close to 18 BB in 263 IP', 'research_needed': ['WWII military service', 'Combat leg injury', 'Use of leg brace'], 'full_statistics': candidate['full_data'] } filename = f"workspace/{candidate['name'].replace(' ', '_').lower()}_research.json" with open(filename, 'w') as f: json.dump(candidate_research, f, indent=2) print(f"Candidate research file saved: {filename}\n") else: print("No WWII-era candidates found with matching statistical profile\n") print("\nStep 3: Searching the HTML content for direct mentions of our target statistics...\n") # Search the entire HTML content for mentions of 18 and 263 html_text = soup.get_text().lower() # Look for any mention of 18 walks or 263 innings if '18' in html_text and '263' in html_text: print("Found both 18 and 263 in the HTML content!") # Find the context around these numbers lines = html_text.split('\n') relevant_lines = [] for line in lines: if '18' in line and '263' in line: relevant_lines.append(line.strip()) if relevant_lines: print(f"\nFound {len(relevant_lines)} lines containing both 18 and 263:") for i, line in enumerate(relevant_lines): print(f"{i+1}. {line[:200]}...") # Check if we have the search summary file summary_file = 'workspace/comprehensive_search_summary.json' if os.path.exists(summary_file): print("Inspecting comprehensive search summary structure...") with open(summary_file, 'r') as f: summary_content = f.read() print(f"Summary file size: {len(summary_content)} characters") # import json import os from bs4 import BeautifulSoup import re # Create workspace directory if it doesn't exist if not os.path.exists('workspace'): os.makedirs('workspace') print("=== ANALYZING BASEBALL-REFERENCE WALK RATE LEADERS FOR WWII VETERAN PITCHER ===\n") print("Objective: Parse the successfully downloaded Baseball-Reference data") print("Target: Pitcher with 18 walks in 263 innings + WWII service + combat leg injury\n") # First, let's inspect what files we have in workspace from the previous search print("Step 1: Inspecting available files in workspace...\n") workspace_files = [] if os.path.exists('workspace'): for file in os.listdir('workspace'): workspace_files.append(file) file_size = os.path.getsize(f'workspace/{file}') print(f"Found: {file} ({file_size:,} bytes)") print(f"\nTotal files available: {len(workspace_files)}\n") # Focus on the successfully downloaded Baseball-Reference walk leaders file walk_leaders_file = 'workspace/baseball_reference_walk_leaders.html' if os.path.exists(walk_leaders_file): print("Step 2: Analyzing Baseball-Reference walk rate leaders data...\n") with open(walk_leaders_file, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f: html_content = f.read() print(f"HTML file size: {len(html_content):,} characters") # Parse the HTML content soup = BeautifulSoup(html_content, 'html.parser') # Look for the main statistics table tables = soup.find_all('table') print(f"Found {len(tables)} tables in the HTML\n") # Analyze each table for historical data for table_idx, table in enumerate(tables): print(f"=== ANALYZING TABLE {table_idx + 1} ===\n") # Get table headers header_row = table.find('tr') if header_row: headers = [th.get_text().strip() for th in header_row.find_all(['th', 'td'])] print(f"Headers: {headers}\n") # Look for columns that might contain our target data year_col = None player_col = None bb_per_9_col = None ip_col = None for i, header in enumerate(headers): header_lower = header.lower() if 'year' in header_lower: year_col = i elif 'player' in header_lower or 'name' in header_lower: player_col = i elif 'bases on balls' in header_lower or 'bb' in header_lower: bb_per_9_col = i elif 'ip' in header_lower or 'innings' in header_lower: ip_col = i print(f"Column indices - Year: {year_col}, Player: {player_col}, BB/9: {bb_per_9_col}, IP: {ip_col}\n") # Get all data rows data_rows = table.find_all('tr')[1:] # Skip header row print(f"Found {len(data_rows)} data rows\n") # Look for WWII-era entries (1940-1950) with very low walk rates wwii_era_pitchers = [] for row_idx, row in enumerate(data_rows[:50]): # Check first 50 rows cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th']) if len(cells) >= len(headers): row_data = [cell.get_text().strip() for cell in cells] # Check if this is a WWII-era entry year = None if year_col is not None and year_col < len(row_data): year_text = row_data[year_col] try: year = int(year_text) except ValueError: continue # Look for 1940s entries if year and 1940 <= year <= 1950: player_name = row_data[player_col] if player_col is not None and player_col < len(row_data) else 'Unknown' bb_per_9 = row_data[bb_per_9_col] if bb_per_9_col is not None and bb_per_9_col < len(row_data) else 'N/A' innings = row_data[ip_col] if ip_col is not None and ip_col < len(row_data) else 'N/A' print(f"WWII-era entry {row_idx + 1}: {year} - {player_name}") print(f" BB/9: {bb_per_9}, IP: {innings}") print(f" Full row: {row_data[:6]}...") # Show first 6 columns # Calculate if this could match our target (18 BB in 263 IP) try: bb_rate = float(bb_per_9) ip_value = float(innings) if innings != 'N/A' else 0 # Our target rate: 18 walks in 263 innings = 0.616 BB/9 target_rate = (18 * 9) / 263 if abs(bb_rate - target_rate) < 0.1: # Very close to target rate print(f" *** POTENTIAL MATCH: BB/9 rate {bb_rate} is very close to target {target_rate:.3f} ***") # Check if innings are close to 263 if abs(ip_value - 263) < 20: # Within 20 innings print(f" ðŸŽ¯ STRONG CANDIDATE: {player_name} ({year})") print(f" BB/9: {bb_rate} (target: {target_rate:.3f})") print(f" IP: {ip_value} (target: 263)") wwii_era_pitchers.append({ 'name': player_name, 'year': year, 'bb_per_9': bb_rate, 'innings': ip_value, 'full_data': row_data }) except ValueError: pass # Skip if we can't parse the numbers print() # Empty line for readability if wwii_era_pitchers: print(f"\n=== FOUND {len(wwii_era_pitchers)} POTENTIAL WWII-ERA CANDIDATES ===\n") for candidate in wwii_era_pitchers: print(f"Candidate: {candidate['name']} ({candidate['year']})") print(f" Statistics: {candidate['bb_per_9']} BB/9 in {candidate['innings']} IP") print(f" Target match: 18 BB in 263 IP (0.616 BB/9)") print() # Now we need to research this specific pitcher for WWII service and leg injury print(f"*** RESEARCHING {candidate['name']} FOR WWII SERVICE AND COMBAT INJURY ***\n") # Save candidate for further research candidate_research = { 'pitcher_name': candidate['name'], 'season_year': candidate['year'], 'bb_per_9_rate': candidate['bb_per_9'], 'innings_pitched': candidate['innings'], 'statistical_match': 'Close to 18 BB in 263 IP', 'research_needed': ['WWII military service', 'Combat leg injury', 'Use of leg brace'], 'full_statistics': candidate['full_data'] } filename = f"workspace/{candidate['name'].replace(' ', '_').lower()}_research.json" with open(filename, 'w') as f: json.dump(candidate_research, f, indent=2) print(f"Candidate research file saved: {filename}\n") else: print("No WWII-era candidates found with matching statistical profile\n") print("\nStep 3: Searching the HTML content for direct mentions of our target statistics...\n") # Search the entire HTML content for mentions of 18 and 263 html_text = soup.get_text().lower() # Look for any mention of 18 walks or 263 innings if '18' in html_text and '263' in html_text: print("Found both 18 and 263 in the HTML content!") # Find the context around these numbers lines = html_text.split('\n') relevant_lines = [] for line in lines: if '18' in line and '263' in line: relevant_lines.append(line.strip()) if relevant_lines: print(f"\nFound {len(relevant_lines)} lines containing both 18 and 263:") for i, line in enumerate(relevant_lines): print(f"{i+1}. {line[:200]}...") # Show first 200 characters elif '18' in html_text: print("Found mentions of 18 in the content") # Count occurrences count_18 = html_text.count('18') print(f"Total occurrences of '18': {count_18}") else: print("No mentions of 18 or 263 found in the HTML content") print("This suggests our target pitcher may not be in the all-time walk rate leaders") else: print("Baseball-Reference walk leaders file not found") print("Available files:") for file in workspace_files: print(f" - {file}") print("\nStep 4: Checking comprehensive search summary for next steps...\n") # Check if we have the search summary file summary_file = 'workspace/comprehensive_search_summary.json' if os.path.exists(summary_file): print("Inspecting comprehensive search summary structure...") with open(summary_file, 'r') as f: summary_content = f.read() print(f"Summary file size: {len(summary_content)} characters") # Parse as JSON to understand structure try: summary_data = json.loads(summary_content) print(f"\nSummary file keys: {list(summary_data.keys())}") # Show the target criteria if 'target_criteria' in summary_data: criteria = summary_data['target_criteria'] print(f"\nTarget criteria:") for key, value in criteria.items(): print(f" {key}: {value}") # Show files created if 'files_created' in summary_data: files_created = summary_data['files_created'] print(f"\nFiles that should have been created: {files_created}") # Check which files actually exist existing_files = [] missing_files = [] for filename in files_created: filepath = f'workspace/{filename}' if os.path.exists(filepath): existing_files.append(filename) else: missing_files.append(filename) print(f"\nActually existing files: {existing_files}") print(f"Missing files: {missing_files}") except json.JSONDecodeError as e: print(f"Error parsing summary file: {e}") print("\n" + "="*80) print("ANALYSIS COMPLETE") print("\nFINDINGS:") print("- Successfully analyzed Baseball-Reference walk rate leaders data") print("- Searched for WWII-era pitchers (1940-1950) with exceptional control") print("- Identified any candidates matching the statistical profile") print("\nNEXT STEPS:") print("1. ### Development Step 1: 1977 Yankees Player Walk Totals: Identify Highest Walker and Record Their At-Bats

**Description**: Search for comprehensive 1977 New York Yankees regular season statistics focusing on individual player walk totals. Target these information sources: (1) Official MLB statistics databases or archives, (2) Baseball-Reference.com historical data for 1977 Yankees roster, (3) Sports statistics websites with detailed seasonal breakdowns, (4) Historical baseball records covering individual player performance metrics. Extract complete batting statistics including walks (BB) and at-bats (AB) for all Yankees players during the 1977 regular season. Identify the player with the highest walk total and record their corresponding at-bat count for verification.

**Use Cases**:
- Sports journalist preparing a retrospective article on the 1977 Yankeesâ€™ plate discipline by automating extraction of walk (BB) and at-bat (AB) statistics for key players.
- Baseball sabermetric researcher integrating 1977 Yankees walk and at-bat data into a player valuation model to compare on-base contributions across the roster.
- Fantasy baseball platform enriching vintage player profiles by scraping 1977 season BB and AB totals for fan leaderboards and historical matchup tools.
- Sports memorabilia e-commerce site validating authenticity of signed items by cross-referencing player season statistics (walks and at-bats) extracted from official archives.
- Data science instructor designing a hands-on web-scraping assignment that uses Baseball-Reference 1977 Yankees data to teach students ETL and analysis workflows.
- Sports television production team generating on-air graphics for a documentary on the 1977 championship season by programmatically retrieving walk and at-bat metrics.
- Machine learning engineer curating a historical baseball dataset to train models on plate discipline trends using automated scraping of 1977 Yankees batting statistics.
- Baseball historian building a searchable digital archive of player performance by importing 1977 Yankees BB and AB data into a relational database for longitudinal studies.

```
import requests
import json
import os
from bs4 import BeautifulSoup
import time

# Create workspace directory if it doesn't exist
if not os.path.exists('workspace'):
os.makedirs('workspace')

print("=== SEARCHING FOR 1977 NEW YORK YANKEES PLAYER STATISTICS ===")
print("Target: Individual player walk (BB) and at-bat (AB) totals for regular season")
print()

# First, let's search for Baseball-Reference data which is the most comprehensive source
# We'll try to find the 1977 Yankees team page

headers = {
'User-Agent': 'Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/91.0.4472.124 Safari/537.36'
}

print("Step 1: Searching Baseball-Reference for 1977 Yankees team statistics...")

# Try to access Baseball-Reference 1977 Yankees page
baseballref_url = "https://www.baseball-reference.com/teams/NYY/1977.shtml"

try:
response = requests.get(baseballref_url, headers=headers, timeout=30)
print(f"Baseball-Reference response status: {response.status_code}")

if response.status_code == 200:
print("Successfully accessed Baseball-Reference 1977 Yankees page")
soup = BeautifulSoup(response.content, 'html.parser')

# Save the raw HTML for analysis
with open('workspace/baseball_reference_1977_yankees.html', 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
f.write(response.text)

print("Raw HTML saved to workspace/baseball_reference_1977_yankees.html")

# Look for batting statistics table
batting_tables = soup.find_all('table', {'id': lambda x: x and 'batting' in x.lower() if x else False})
if not batting_tables:
batting_tables = soup.find_all('table', {'class': lambda x: x and 'stats_table' in ' '.join(x) if x else False})

print(f"Found {len(batting_tables)} potential batting statistics tables")

# Also look for any table that might contain player statistics
all_tables = soup.find_all('table')
print(f"Total tables found on page: {len(all_tables)}")

# Look for table headers that might indicate batting stats
batting_data = []
for i, table in enumerate(all_tables[:10]): # Check first 10 tables
headers = table.find_all('th')
header_text = [th.get_text().strip() for th in headers]

print(f"\nTable {i+1} headers: {header_text[:10]}") # Show first 10 headers

# Check if this table contains batting statistics
batting_indicators = ['BB', 'AB', 'Player', 'Name', 'Walks', 'At Bats', 'H', 'R', 'RBI']
has_batting_stats = any(indicator in ' '.join(header_text) for indicator in batting_indicators)

if has_batting_stats:
print(f"*** TABLE {i+1} APPEARS TO CONTAIN BATTING STATISTICS ***")

# Extract rows from this table
rows = table.find_all('tr')
print(f"Table has {len(rows)} rows")

if len(rows) > 1: # Has header + data rows
# Get first few data rows as examples
for j, row in enumerate(rows[1:6]): # Skip header, get first 5 data rows
cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th'])
cell_data = [cell.get_text().strip() for cell in cells]
print(f" Row {j+1}: {cell_data[:8]}...") # Show first 8 columns

batting_data.append({
'table_index': i+1,
'headers': header_text,
'row_count': len(rows),
'sample_rows': [[cell.get_text().strip() for cell in row.find_all(['td', 'th'])] for row in rows[1:6]]
})

# Save batting data analysis
analysis_data = {
'source': 'Baseball-Reference 1977 Yankees',
'url': baseballref_url,
'access_successful': True,
'total_tables_found': len(all_tables),
'batting_tables_identified': len(batting_data),
'batting_data_analysis': batting_data,
'timestamp': time.strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')
}

with open('workspace/baseball_reference_analysis.json', 'w') as f:
json.dump(analysis_data, f, indent=2)

print(f"\n=== INITIAL ANALYSIS COMPLETE ===")
print(f"Found {len(batting_data)} tables with potential batting statistics")
print("Detailed analysis saved to workspace/baseball_reference_analysis.json")

else:
print(f"Failed to access Baseball-Reference: HTTP {response.status_code}")

except Exception as e:
print(f"Error accessing Baseball-Reference: {str(e)}")

print("\n" + "="*60)
print("NEXT STEPS:")
print("1. Analyze the extracted table data to identify player walk statistics")
print("2. Search additional sources if needed (MLB.com, other statistics sites)")
print("3. Compile complete 1977 Yankees roster with BB and AB totals")
print("4. Identify player with highest walk total and their AB count")
```

### Development Step 2: 1977 Yankees Walk Totals and At-Bat Statistics: Identify Highest Walker

**Description**: Search for comprehensive 1977 New York Yankees regular season statistics focusing on individual player walk totals. Target these information sources: (1) Official MLB statistics databases or archives, (2) Baseball-Reference.com historical data for 1977 Yankees roster, (3) Sports statistics websites with detailed seasonal breakdowns, (4) Historical baseball records covering individual player performance metrics. Extract complete batting statistics including walks (BB) and at-bats (AB) for all Yankees players during the 1977 regular season. Identify the player with the highest walk total and record their corresponding at-bat count for verification.

**Use Cases**:
- Automated sports analytics workflow for a baseball research lab that extracts 1977 Yankees walk and at-bat data from official MLB archives to feed into sabermetric models.
- Fantasy baseball platform ingestion pipeline that scrapes Baseball-Reference to import historical walk totals and at-bat counts for recreating retro league drafts and player valuation.
- Sports journalism verification tool that pulls archived Yankees batting tables to fact-check player on-base performance in feature stories on the 1977 World Series season.
- Academic statistical study on plate discipline trends using extracted walk and at-bat figures for the 1977 New York Yankees roster to support peer-reviewed publications.
- Interactive museum exhibit dashboard that automatically loads player BB and AB stats from 1977 to power visual timelines and fan-driven exploration of Yankees history.
- Sports betting analytics system incorporating historical walk-to-at-bat ratios from the 1977 season to refine predictive models for modern game odds.
- Digital memorabilia marketplace integration that auto-populates player performance metadata (walks and at-bats) from trusted archives to enhance trading card listings.
- Enterprise data pipeline for a sports data provider that standardizes extracted BB and AB columns from multiple sources into a cloud warehouse for client reporting APIs.

```
import json
import os
from bs4 import BeautifulSoup
import re

# First, let's inspect the structure of the saved analysis file to understand what data we have
analysis_file = 'workspace/baseball_reference_analysis.json'

print("=== ANALYZING SAVED BASEBALL-REFERENCE DATA ===")
print("Step 1: Inspecting the structure of saved analysis file...")

if os.path.exists(analysis_file):
with open(analysis_file, 'r') as f:
analysis_data = json.load(f)

print(f"\nAnalysis file keys: {list(analysis_data.keys())}")
print(f"Source: {analysis_data.get('source', 'Unknown')}")
print(f"URL: {analysis_data.get('url', 'Unknown')}")
print(f"Access successful: {analysis_data.get('access_successful', False)}")
print(f"Total tables found: {analysis_data.get('total_tables_found', 0)}")
print(f"Batting tables identified: {analysis_data.get('batting_tables_identified', 0)}")

# Examine the batting data analysis structure
if 'batting_data_analysis' in analysis_data:
batting_data = analysis_data['batting_data_analysis']
print(f"\nFound {len(batting_data)} batting data tables to analyze")

# Inspect each batting table
for i, table_data in enumerate(batting_data):
print(f"\n--- Table {table_data.get('table_index', i+1)} Analysis ---")
headers = table_data.get('headers', [])
print(f"Headers ({len(headers)}): {headers}")
print(f"Row count: {table_data.get('row_count', 0)}")

# Look for BB (walks) and AB (at-bats) columns
bb_index = None
ab_index = None
player_index = None

for j, header in enumerate(headers):
header_clean = header.strip().upper()
if header_clean == 'BB' or 'WALK' in header_clean:
bb_index = j
print(f"*** Found BB (walks) column at index {j}: '{header}' ***")
elif header_clean == 'AB' or 'AT BAT' in header_clean or header_clean == 'AT-BAT':
ab_index = j
print(f"*** Found AB (at-bats) column at index {j}: '{header}' ***")
elif 'PLAYER' in header_clean or 'NAME' in header_clean or header_clean == 'NAME':
player_index = j
print(f"*** Found player name column at index {j}: '{header}' ***")

# Examine sample rows
sample_rows = table_data.get('sample_rows', [])
print(f"\nSample rows ({len(sample_rows)}):")
for k, row in enumerate(sample_rows):
print(f" Row {k+1}: {row}")

# If we found BB and AB columns, highlight those values
if bb_index is not None and len(row) > bb_index:
print(f" BB value at index {bb_index}: '{row[bb_index]}'")
if ab_index is not None and len(row) > ab_index:
print(f" AB value at index {ab_index}: '{row[ab_index]}'")
if player_index is not None and len(row) > player_index:
print(f" Player name at index {player_index}: '{row[player_index]}'")

# Store column indices for later use
table_data['bb_column_index'] = bb_index
table_data['ab_column_index'] = ab_index
table_data['player_column_index'] = player_index

# Determine if this table is suitable for extraction
if bb_index is not None and ab_index is not None and player_index is not None:
print(f"\n*** TABLE {table_data.get('table_index', i+1)} IS SUITABLE FOR EXTRACTION ***")
print(f"Has all required columns: Player({player_index}), BB({bb_index}), AB({ab_index})")
table_data['suitable_for_extraction'] = True
else:
print(f"\n--- Table {table_data.get('table_index', i+1)} missing required columns ---")
missing = []
if bb_index is None: missing.append('BB')
if ab_index is None: missing.append('AB')
if player_index is None: missing.append('Player')
print(f"Missing: {', '.join(missing)}")
table_data['suitable_for_extraction'] = False

# Save updated analysis with column indices
with open('workspace/baseball_reference_analysis_updated.json', 'w') as f:
json.dump(analysis_data, f, indent=2)

print(f"\n=== ANALYSIS COMPLETE ===")
print("Updated analysis saved to workspace/baseball_reference_analysis_updated.json")

else:
print(f"Error: Analysis file not found at {analysis_file}")
print("Available files in workspace:")
if os.path.exists('workspace'):
for file in os.listdir('workspace'):
print(f" - {file}")
else:
print(" - workspace directory not found")

print("\n" + "="*60)
print("NEXT STEP: Parse the actual HTML file to extract complete player statistics")
print("Will focus on tables identified as suitable for extraction")
```

**Description**: Search for comprehensive 1977 New York Yankees regular season statistics focusing on individual player walk totals. **Use Cases**:
- Automated sports analytics pipeline for a baseball statistics website that scrapes historical MLB table data, filters out summary rows, and ranks players by walk-to-at-bat ratios.
- Fantasy baseball app backend for generating custom leaderboards from Baseball-Reference tables by extracting individual player walk totals and at-bat counts while excluding aggregate team lines.

```
import json
import os

# Following the tester's feedback, I need to fix the filtering logic to exclude team totals and summary rows
# First, let's inspect the saved results file to understand the current data structure

results_file = 'workspace/1977_yankees_walk_leaders.json'

print("=== CORRECTING 1977 YANKEES WALK LEADER IDENTIFICATION ===")
print("Issue: Previous extraction included 'Team Totals' as top player")
print("Solution: Filter out team summary rows and identify actual individual player\n")

# Check if results file exists and inspect its structure
if os.path.exists(results_file):
print("Step 1: Inspecting saved results file structure...")

with open(results_file, 'r') as f:
results_data = json.load(f)

print(f"Results file keys: {list(results_data.keys())}")

if 'all_players_by_walks' in results_data:
print(f"\nFound {len(results_data['all_players_by_walks'])} players in saved results")
print("\nTop 10 players (including problematic data):")

for player_data in results_data['all_players_by_walks']:
player_name = player_data.get('player', 'Unknown')
bb = player_data.get('bb', 0)
ab = player_data.get('ab', 0)
rank = player_data.get('rank', 0)
print(f"{rank:2d}. {player_name:<25} - BB: {bb:3d}, AB: {ab:3d}")

# Identify problematic entries
if 'total' in player_name.lower() or 'team' in player_name.lower():
print(f" *** TEAM SUMMARY ROW - SHOULD BE EXCLUDED ***")
else:
print(f"Results file not found: {results_file}")
print("Available files in workspace:")
if os.path.exists('workspace'):
for file in os.listdir('workspace'):
print(f" - {file}")

print("\n" + "="*60)
print("Step 2: Re-processing data to exclude team totals and summary rows...")

# Load the original analysis data to re-extract with proper filtering
analysis_file = 'workspace/baseball_reference_analysis_updated.json'

if not os.path.exists(analysis_file):
print(f"Analysis file not found: {analysis_file}")
exit()

with open(analysis_file, 'r') as f:
analysis_data = json.load(f)

# Re-load and parse HTML with improved filtering
html_file = 'workspace/baseball_reference_1977_yankees.html'

if not os.path.exists(html_file):
print(f"HTML file not found: {html_file}")
exit()

print(f"Loading HTML file: {html_file}")

with open(html_file, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
html_content = f.read()

from bs4 import BeautifulSoup
import re

soup = BeautifulSoup(html_content, 'html.parser')
all_tables = soup.find_all('table')

print(f"Found {len(all_tables)} tables in HTML\n")

# Find suitable tables from analysis
suitable_tables = []
if 'batting_data_analysis' in analysis_data:
for table_data in analysis_data['batting_data_analysis']:
if table_data.get('suitable_for_extraction', False):
suitable_tables.append(table_data)

print(f"Using {len(suitable_tables)} suitable tables for extraction")

# Extract player statistics with improved filtering
all_players = {}

# Define filter terms to exclude team totals and summary rows
exclude_terms = ['team', 'total', 'totals', 'average', 'avg', 'league', 'al ', 'nl ', 'summary']

for table_info in suitable_tables:
table_index = table_info.get('table_index', 0) - 1
player_col = table_info.get('player_column_index')
bb_col = table_info.get('bb_column_index')
ab_col = table_info.get('ab_column_index')

print(f"\n--- Processing Table {table_index + 1} ---")
print(f"Player col: {player_col}, BB col: {bb_col}, AB col: {ab_col}")

if table_index < len(all_tables) and all(col is not None for col in [player_col, bb_col, ab_col]):
table = all_tables[table_index]
rows = table.find_all('tr')

print(f"Table has {len(rows)} rows")

# Process data rows (skip header)
extracted_count = 0
for i, row in enumerate(rows[1:], 1):
cells = row.find_all(['td', 'th'])

if len(cells) > max(player_col, bb_col, ab_col):
player_name = cells[player_col].get_text().strip()
bb_text = cells[bb_col].get_text().strip()
ab_text = cells[ab_col].get_text().strip()

# Enhanced filtering logic
if player_name and bb_text and ab_text:
# Check if player name contains exclude terms
player_name_lower = player_name.lower()
is_excluded = any(term in player_name_lower for term in exclude_terms)

if is_excluded:
print(f" Row {i}: EXCLUDED - {player_name} (contains summary terms)")
continue

# Clean numeric data
try:
bb_clean = re.sub(r'[^0-9]', '', bb_text)
ab_clean = re.sub(r'[^0-9]', '', ab_text)

if bb_clean and ab_clean:
bb_value = int(bb_clean)
ab_value = int(ab_clean)

# Filter criteria: reasonable AB count for individual players
if 20 <= ab_value <= 700: # Reasonable range for MLB player
extracted_count += 1
print(f" Row {i}: INCLUDED - {player_name:<20} BB: {bb_value:3d}, AB: {ab_value:3d}")

# Store or update player data (take higher values if duplicate)
if player_name in all_players:
if bb_value > all_players[player_name]['BB']:
all_players[player_name] = {'BB': bb_value, 'AB': ab_value}
else:
all_players[player_name] = {'BB': bb_value, 'AB': ab_value}
else:
print(f" Row {i}: EXCLUDED - {player_name} (AB={ab_value} outside range)")

except ValueError:
print(f" Row {i}: EXCLUDED - {player_name} (invalid numeric data)")
continue

print(f"Extracted {extracted_count} valid players from Table {table_index + 1}")

print(f"\n=== CORRECTED 1977 YANKEES PLAYER STATISTICS ===")
print(f"Total individual players extracted: {len(all_players)}")

if len(all_players) == 0:
print("ERROR: No players extracted with current filtering criteria")
print("This suggests the data structure may be different than expected")
exit()

# Sort players by walks in descending order
players_by_walks = sorted(all_players.items(), key=lambda x: x[1]['BB'], reverse=True)

print("\n=== INDIVIDUAL PLAYERS RANKED BY WALKS (BB) ===")
for rank, (player, stats) in enumerate(players_by_walks, 1):
print(f"{rank:2d}. {player:<25} - BB: {stats['BB']:3d}, AB: {stats['AB']:3d}")

# Identify the correct answer
if players_by_walks:
top_player = players_by_walks[0]
player_name = top_player[0]
player_stats = top_player[1]

print(f"\n" + "="*60)
print("=== CORRECTED ANSWER ===")
print(f"1977 New York Yankees player with most walks:")
print(f"Player: {player_name}")
print(f"Walks (BB): {player_stats['BB']}")
print(f"At-Bats (AB): {player_stats['AB']}")
print("="*60)

# Save corrected results
corrected_results = {
'question': 'Which 1977 New York Yankees player had the most walks and what was their at-bat count?',
'corrected_answer': {
'player_name': player_name,
'walks_bb': player_stats['BB'],
'at_bats_ab': player_stats['AB']
},
'source': 'Baseball-Reference.com 1977 Yankees team page',
'url': analysis_data.get('url', ''),
'top_10_individual_players': [
{'rank': i+1, 'player': name, 'bb': stats['BB'], 'ab': stats['AB']}
for i, (name, stats) in enumerate(players_by_walks[:10])
],
'total_individual_players': len(all_players),
'filtering_applied': 'Excluded team totals, summary rows, and players with unrealistic AB counts',
'exclude_terms_used': exclude_terms
}

with open('workspace/1977_yankees_corrected_walk_leaders.json', 'w') as f:
json.dump(corrected_results, f, indent=2)

print(f"\nCorrected results saved to workspace/1977_yankees_corrected_walk_leaders.json")

else:
print("\nERROR: No individual players found after filtering")
